  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e36c4692-4d7f-454f-bb05-aa56b279efea'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText14808438488112670522" style="display:none">The Icemark is a kingdom in grave danger. Its king has been killed in battle, its enemy lies in wait, and its fate rests on the shoulders of one girl. Thirrin Freer Strong-in-the-Arm Lindenshield, a beautiful princess and an intrepid warrior, must find a way to protect her land from a terrible invasion. She will forge an extraordinary alliance of noble Snow Leopards, ancient Vampires, and ferocious Wolf-folk. She will find unexpected strength in her friendship with a young warlock. And she will lead her allies to victory with her fierce battle cry: "Blood! Blast! And Fire!"</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2011-reading">2011-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60213341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18259213925425584409">Cry of the Icemark was a stirring military fantasy adventure. The author really took the time to bring the cultures of this novel to life. I could see that Icemark people seemed to be modelled after the Scandinavians, while Thyrrin's mother's peoples, the Hypollitan must have been based on the Amazons. And the Polipontans seemed to be like the Roman Empire. The battle scenes were fantastic--thrilling and very well-written. I got the impression that Mr. Hill took these elements very seriously and</span>
  <span id="freeText18259213925425584409" style="display:none">Cry of the Icemark was a stirring military fantasy adventure. The author really took the time to bring the cultures of this novel to life. I could see that Icemark people seemed to be modelled after the Scandinavians, while Thyrrin's mother's peoples, the Hypollitan must have been based on the Amazons. And the Polipontans seemed to be like the Roman Empire. The battle scenes were fantastic--thrilling and very well-written. I got the impression that Mr. Hill took these elements very seriously and worked hard to get this part right and make it feel realistic. And I appreciated that, and I am sure that his younger readers probably do as well. Although not excessively gory, I felt all the inherent threat and bloody nature of battle. The element of loss is very evident in this story, and I definitely could appreciate the horrible odds that Thyrrin's people faced with an enormous invading force pitted against their smaller country. However, the Icemark people quickly proved that they wouldn't easily be conquered. Along with their fierce nature, there were elements of their rich sense of family and tradition, many aspects that would have been destroyed or wiped away by the Polipontans, who cared nothing for other cultures, only the assimilation of their lands and raw resources.<br /><br />Thyrrin is a young heroine that I just loved. She was born to be a queen, and she showed a multi-facetedness to her character that brought her to vivid life. She's very strong and the kind of leader you want to have when you are facing a mammoth invading force who wants to wipe your people off the face of the earth. On the other hand, it's clear that she is very young and still learning a lot about leadership, courage, and humanity. I really wanted to give her a hug for all that she dealt with in this novel. I loved her friend, Oskan, Witch's Son too. He had a mystique, and a wisdom that was much greater than his young years. I also loved his wry sense of humor and the fact that he never took himself too importantly, despite his incredible latent power. He was a good companion to Thyrrin, able to deal with her sometimes hot-headed arrogance, and to soothe her very recognizable fears with the voice of reason and comfort when she seemed like she couldn't handle one more burden. In fact, most of the characters were well-drawn and excellently narrated by Heather O'Neill. This book really got me sucked in. I found myself cheering for Thyrrin and her warriors (the Hypollitan warrior women were freaking awesome), and hating General Scipio Bellaron. I loved the werewolves and the snow leopards, both groups having a ton of personality. The vampires were nicely creepy, and the wood folk (like the Green men and nature spirits of Celtic/Norse mythology) added a sense of majestic awe to this story. This book would have great as just a straight military historical fantasy, but the supernatural elements elevated it to an even more interesting level. <br /><br /><br />There was so much to like about this story. It really got me revved up. I was excited to listen to it, and sad but satisfied when it ended. It was definitely a five star listen for this reader. I look forward to the reading the other books in this series. Recommended!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18259213925425584409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_889664821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/889664821" />
    <a title="Drakaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29917936-drakaina"><img alt="Drakaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395618733p2/29917936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/889664821?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drakaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drakaina" href="/user/show/29917936-drakaina">Drakaina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Very young readers. Certainly NOT FOR FANS OF MILITARY  HISTORY unless they want a huge facepalm</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29917936-drakaina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29917936-drakaina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer889664821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11372451534005249757">All right, I am definitely out of the age range of this book and I have apparently outgrown the phase when one-dimension characters in a straightforward plot can win my heart. Now, could they ever? I'm not so sure, but the five-star reviews from young readers show that the book is appreciated and even loved.<br/><br/>I decided to give it two stars instead of one for one simple reason: the plot and characters can earn one star at best (since there is no "no-stars" option), while I do see some potential in </span>
  <span id="freeText11372451534005249757" style="display:none">All right, I am definitely out of the age range of this book and I have apparently outgrown the phase when one-dimension characters in a straightforward plot can win my heart. Now, could they ever? I'm not so sure, but the five-star reviews from young readers show that the book is appreciated and even loved.<br /><br />I decided to give it two stars instead of one for one simple reason: the plot and characters can earn one star at best (since there is no "no-stars" option), while I do see some potential in the author's style (at times) and also in a number of plot/world devices, such as the werewolf relay system or the general idea of introducing a scholar who observes the world, records histories etc. I must admit that I quite liked the way the vampires were presented as the bored, tired with immortality and yet clinging to their existence beings (if only they had served anything at all in the plot and their characters had any individuality - well, the latter applies to just every single character in the book).<br /><br />However, all such things cannot save a plot as thin as the most luxurious vellum, or characters that are as bland as it gets. The plot moves from one predictable event to another, and the characters are characterless pawns on a chessboard with a set game. I wonder if anyone at any point doubted that Thirrin would persuade the potential allies to joining her, let alone if anyone anticipated the outcome of any of the battles. Moreover: the logic of the plot escapes me. First the whole city is evacuated and the inhabitants make a tiresome march to the safety of the north, to escape invasion. Apart from the fact that this is damn stupid, it also has no consequences: the capital is taken by the enemy (well, it was EMPTY), who then leaves it (we learn later that the ghosts had some part in driving the enemy out, which actually could be a nice touch, if the author had written it better), and gets annihilated in a battle in the forest. However, when the army goes back in a matter of weeks (having the whole populace of a big city relocated to a smaller one without any economic problems whatsoever), there is no sign of the battle, even though all those corpses covered in snow and ice should make a gruesome view. For some time the capital is empty but the Enemy does not think about repopulating it (they don't have to storm it anymore, since it's EMPTY), so conveniently the Icemarkians come down and simply march in, and the city is fully functionable despite its abandonment in the middle of a very hard winter. Then the small province of the north supplies the army with food, fodder and anything else, the drafted army performs like a professional one after several weeks of training, we get a tedious and over-extended (not to mention unconvincing to downright stupid from the military point of view) description of the battle of <s>Minas Tirith </s> Frostmarris and the book ends.<br /><br />At first glance I expected to enjoy the world: the combination of a developed <s>Roman</s> Polipontian Empire, with cannons and muskets, with a <s>Vikingland</s> Icemark featuring some Viking and some Celtic elements, the <s>Amazons</s> Hyppolitans relocated to the north, and some kind of Greek-like south was promising. Add to it sufficiently original werewolves and vampires - all this looks quite well. If only these lands were inhabited by people and not stereotypes... And if the author had not fallen into one of my most hated pits: of creating a wise, old and perfect race of talking animals. I could not bear the Snow Leopards at all, sorry fans. Still, the idea to use as many cultures as possible is a good one, but please Mr. Hill, add some life to your world and characters!<br /><br />And now comes the worst: unlike many people who wrote reviews here I AM a fan of military history (from antiquity to the 19th century), and what I got deserved a huge laugh at best but mostly a huge facepalm. The author is an archaeologist (it shows, but it does not guarantee good writing), but has no idea about strategy, tactics, logistics and warfare in general. Moreover, he makes the mistake (beginner's perhaps) that he mostly multiplies the numbers of troops instead of thinking about tactics; and what is even worse, he declares throughout the book that the evil and cruel general of the Enemy, a certain Scipio Bellorum, is a military genius. The problem is, Mr. Bellorum's tactics are as naive and silly as it gets, and any army would have him hung or murdered for the way he treats his officers, in the matter of weeks. A lesson for Mr. Hill to learn from history books: all great commanders who lasted long were loved by their armies, not just feared, and certainly not feared for their madness and cruelty - this generally guarantees quick mutiny, even if the captain wins battles.<br /><br />Oh, and I forgot to say that a small city with a tiny garrison withstands ten days of siege when their walls had been breached in several places by a huge army. The army cannot take the city despite the military genius of their commander. And no, the inhabitants don't set fire to their city. Nothing as spectacular, they are JUST SO BRAVE that this alone is enough to keep thousands of legionaries at bay. And mind you, this is not Tolkien, this is supposed to be realistic.<br /><br />And this is it: the book is full of paper characters who impersonate certain traits, without any hint at psychology, without any doubts. Even the scene when Oskan has to choose between being a Black Witch or a White Witch is predictable and devoid of dramatism. There is no single traitor or badass in Icemark, there is no place for good Polypontians. I don't know, maybe this changes in the sequels, but I am not sure if I am going to check it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11372451534005249757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17719983144991043715" style="display:none">I bought this book last 2010 in a book fair at my school and after reading it, set it aside. But now that I rummaged through my library and saw it again, I decided to read it. Excellent made and perfectly-written! <br />I'm not a fan of war books, but because of this masterpiece, it made a boring war story to a suspense one that'll make you turn the pages non-stop! Anyone can totally relate to them.<br /> <br />Thirrin Freer Strong-in-the-Arm Lindenshield is a fourteen year old girl who is the princess of the Icemark kingdom. A strong and fierce girl who'll do anything to save her kingdom against the conquerors. Full of action, adventure, romance, drama and many others, readers would totally love! That's why I'm giving this five stars! <br /><br /><b> A MUST READ! </b> </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_70169618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70169618" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1486865-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442463581p2/1486865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70169618?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/1486865-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1486865-scott?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1486865-scott?shelf=market-research">market-research</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70169618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9361840952835204707">From the outset, this story seems contrived and not very deeply thought out. The story begins with a detailed history-book style narrative of the kingdom of Icemark (breaking the vaunted "show, don't tell" rule), and then moves on into some very "staged" plot devices. Example: In the second chapter, the "werewolf" our heroine has captured and brought back to her father's castle (Aren't werewolves supposed to change back into human form at some point? If not, it's not "were," it's just a "wolf.")</span>
  <span id="freeText9361840952835204707" style="display:none">From the outset, this story seems contrived and not very deeply thought out. The story begins with a detailed history-book style narrative of the kingdom of Icemark (breaking the vaunted "show, don't tell" rule), and then moves on into some very "staged" plot devices. Example: In the second chapter, the "werewolf" our heroine has captured and brought back to her father's castle (Aren't werewolves supposed to change back into human form at some point? If not, it's not "were," it's just a "wolf.") announces to everyone in the hall that he is king of the werewolves. (Seems to me that if you were a king in the clutches of your enemies, you might not want to make a big announcement of that fact.) I didn't read much further than that. Because this story is quite transparent and contrived, it might make a nice introduction for very young readers into the realm of fantasy literature - but older readers and adults are likely to be bored with it pretty quickly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9361840952835204707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_308330306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308330306" />
    <a title="Em-nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5359600-em-nat"><img alt="Em-nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577732911p2/5359600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308330306?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em-nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em-nat" href="/user/show/5359600-em-nat">Em-nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439686266" href="/book/show/1292327.The_Cry_of_the_Icemark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308330306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10676648506453000215">"Cry of the Icemark" is one of the most sickeningly misogynistic YA stories I have ever had the misfortune of reading. I’m surprised at how many readers have managed to delude themselves into thinking that Hill has written a female role-model in Therin, considering how antagonistic and hateful she is toward all the other female characters she meets in the book (literally, all of them), and her constant insistence on surrounding herself with no one but men. Even her animal companions are male. At</span>
  <span id="freeText10676648506453000215" style="display:none">"Cry of the Icemark" is one of the most sickeningly misogynistic YA stories I have ever had the misfortune of reading. I’m surprised at how many readers have managed to delude themselves into thinking that Hill has written a female role-model in Therin, considering how antagonistic and hateful she is toward all the other female characters she meets in the book (literally, all of them), and her constant insistence on surrounding herself with no one but men. Even her animal companions are male. At one point, Therin states that women in a positions of power are UNNATURAL. Her own advisor has to remind her that she is in fact a woman in a position of power. Her answer is that she is a special case because SHE was raised by a man. What?<br /><br />To top it all off, this author writes with the verbal capacity of a 14-year-old emulating Tolkien and manages to make even battle scenes tedious and boring. All of the characters were cookie-cutter personality types that I cared nothing about. I really can’t understand the good reviews for this book. It's like "Twilight" for wannabe sword-and-sorcery buffs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10676648506453000215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_595610067" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amy by: </span>
      YL Jordan
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=strong-females">strong-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=books-i-wouldn-t-mind-owning">books-i-wouldn-t-mind-owning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=juvenile-fiction">juvenile-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595610067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8112897204719181441">Well, I know which camp I fall into! I loved it!<br/>Mostly. <br/><i>The Cry of the Icemark</i> tells a richly imaginative tale about a young queen trying to save her country from foreign invaders by collecting allies from the mythical creatures around her. (Werewolves, vampires, ents....er, tree people, etc.) <br/>I definitely approached it as a children's book as it reminded me a lot of Narnia which might explain why I didn't feel as frustrated as many other reviews seem to to with details like accuracy with battle</span>
  <span id="freeText8112897204719181441" style="display:none">Well, I know which camp I fall into! I loved it!<br />Mostly. <br /><i>The Cry of the Icemark</i> tells a richly imaginative tale about a young queen trying to save her country from foreign invaders by collecting allies from the mythical creatures around her. (Werewolves, vampires, ents....er, tree people, etc.) <br />I definitely approached it as a children's book as it reminded me a lot of Narnia which might explain why I didn't feel as frustrated as many other reviews seem to to with details like accuracy with battle strategy. I found it an enjoyable book of empowerment and myth that I could see reading out loud to my niece and nephew. The author packs lots of creative themes into it (such as loss, leadership, and the tension between faith and "science") without ever feeling over the top. <br />That said, I don't think I would enjoy this if I just read it for my own pleasure, without imagining it as aimed at a younger audience. The heroine feels extremely juvenile at times and her impulsiveness occasionally made me cringe. While I looked forward to picking the story up again when I put it down, I never felt anxious about what would happen next. And honestly, the love interest was kinda...meh. (Is there a reason we didn't find out who his father was? Or did we and I just zoned out whenever the story focused on him?)<br />I did love the cats.<br />But the heroine is truly what holds this story together. I liked how gutsy she was. She was exactly the sort of female heroine I'd like to give to younger female readers. She really kicks butt and takes names and remains extremely sensitive to her dignity (to the point of being a character flaw.) <br />A nice alternative to Tamora Pierce. <br /><br /><b>Pre-Review</b><br />*Reads synopsis*<br />Blink.<br />*Looks at reviews*<br />5 stars!<br />1 star.<br />5 stars!<br />5 stars!<br />1 star.<br /><br />So...I'm going to go out on a limb here and guess that this is one of those books you either hate or love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8112897204719181441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_65474750" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65474750" />
    <a title="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you"><img alt="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436762808p2/2082345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65474750?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" href="/user/show/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you">Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=own-ab">own-ab</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65474750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6285501070699511344">I'm not a big fan of war books, but I gave this one a try because I thought there would be more to it. There wasn't. The characters were intriguing, and some of them likable, but they had absolutely no development. One could argue that Thirrin grows stronger etc. but really...she was strong from the very beginning, and she never became any less arrogant, or any more likable. Then there was Oskan, the love friend/possible love interest who really was more of a slave for Thirrin to boss around tha</span>
  <span id="freeText6285501070699511344" style="display:none">I'm not a big fan of war books, but I gave this one a try because I thought there would be more to it. There wasn't. The characters were intriguing, and some of them likable, but they had absolutely no development. One could argue that Thirrin grows stronger etc. but really...she was strong from the very beginning, and she never became any less arrogant, or any more likable. Then there was Oskan, the love friend/possible love interest who really was more of a slave for Thirrin to boss around than anything else. I mean, I spent the whole book waiting for them to get together, and they NEVER DID! And then the next book in the trilogy POOF, they're married? Come on. <br /><br />It was all just meaningless action, or boring explainations. There was no character related interest. There were LOTS of characters, which annoyed me--switching back and forth between characters so much, even minor characters who were in the book for about five pages. <br /><br />Sure, the concept was original, and the world created intrguing, but I felt no connection to the story or characters and often found myself saying, "When will something INTERESTING happen?" When will the characters start acting like real poeple instead of peices on a chessboard. Answer: Never. <br /><br />And then there was the ending. It was so abrupt that for a while I thought maybe my copy was missing some pages or something, but nope. It just ends randomly in the middle of a scene with no real resolution to the characters. <br /><br />This book just really annoyed me, and unless you enjoy war books with absolutely no plot-line other than mindless action, don't waste your time reading this 400-something page book of yawns.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6285501070699511344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_494604469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/494604469" />
    <a title="Amanda Duarte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8383355-amanda-duarte"><img alt="Amanda Duarte" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494604469?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Duarte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Duarte" href="/user/show/8383355-amanda-duarte">Amanda Duarte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494604469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7173174568935915625">I do not recommend this book if you are someone who is a fan of Tamora Pierce and other quality authors of the fantasy realm. The characters are flat, bland, entirely undeveloped and unoriginal, and half of them can't seem to decide what sort of overall voice they will have in the entire book. The young Thirrin, and mind you this is a 13-year-old-who-turns-14-in-the-book, is nothing more than a royal brat. She constantly loses her temper with absolutely no consequences to follow, and while I lov</span>
  <span id="freeText7173174568935915625" style="display:none">I do not recommend this book if you are someone who is a fan of Tamora Pierce and other quality authors of the fantasy realm. The characters are flat, bland, entirely undeveloped and unoriginal, and half of them can't seem to decide what sort of overall voice they will have in the entire book. The young Thirrin, and mind you this is a 13-year-old-who-turns-14-in-the-book, is nothing more than a royal brat. She constantly loses her temper with absolutely no consequences to follow, and while I love a female heroin who comes into her own I find it very unbelievable for her to have such an innate ability to acquire allies at the drop of a hat, move armies to their utmost potential without any advice from more experienced housecarls at her age. Really the only believable portion about her was her inability to understand why Oskan's actions irked her so through the wonderfully rosy glasses of puberty and even that gets old before you're halfway done with the book because there's no self examination by the character with which to form the resolution that yes she's attracted to the boy! Much of the story is very much glossed over, with a lot of telling without much expansion upon emotions, reactions... it's the naked itinerary of what could have been a very expansive and emotional epic, but I don't even want to give the author even that much credit, for he also seems to drop rather misogynistic viewpoints in the juxtposition of Icemark's very Norse yet somehow women aren't treated as housekeepers culture with the Hypolitan women rule the roost pov to which Thirrin finds "barbaric". The story seems to tease you with possible sub-plots of the rather aloof (and let's face it, just completely absent) thoughts of the Basilea, Thirrin's aunt, but it's then tossed away as the plot hurries on and on to rather repetitive descriptions of battle scenes that really aren't as exciting or sitting-on-the-edge-of-the-seat as one would hope. In addition the author seems to have a fascination with the number 100, which had appeared four or five times in the span of two short (like 2-3 sentence short) paragraphs as well as having to be the number of the king who rules one of the more animalistic allies Thirrin picks up. Other common (read modern) turns of phrases turn up in the novel which only distract you from the Norse/Greek/Roman/Anglo-Saxon world you are desperately trying to immerse yourself in. Let's be honest here, "new skin cells forming" is not a phrase I want to see in a novel set in a time where it would be perfectly reasonable to see Beowulf walking through the door of the Great Hall.<br /><br />Bottom line, this is no book to waste your time on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7173174568935915625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText1504643262692549379" style="display:none">This is tricky because as a children's book (which I think it is - with the main character being 13 when the story starts) I think this is a solid 4 star as I think it is perhaps lacking in a few areas of world and character building. <div id="review_2067210489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067210489" />
    <a title="Abbey &quot;Burner of Boys in Bear Suits&quot; Flentje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5626921-abbey-burner-of-boys-in-bear-suits-flentje"><img alt="Abbey &quot;Burner of Boys in Bear Suits&quot; Flentje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569383307p2/5626921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067210489?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbey &quot;Burner of Boys in Bear Suits&quot; Flentje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbey &quot;Burner of Boys in Bear Suits&quot; Flentje" href="/user/show/5626921-abbey-burner-of-boys-in-bear-suits-flentje">Abbey &quot;Burner of Boys in Bear Suits&quot; Flentje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439686266" href="/book/show/1292327.The_Cry_of_the_Icemark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5626921-abbey-burner-of-boys-in-bear-suits-flentje?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5626921-abbey-burner-of-boys-in-bear-suits-flentje?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5626921-abbey-burner-of-boys-in-bear-suits-flentje?shelf=ugh">ugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067210489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13681902047366456735">I really wanted to like this book. I really did because fantasy is my favorite genre to read. The concept sounded intriguing, with a warrior girl as the lead protagonist and lots of intense battles. The idea reminded me a bit of Arya Stark.<br/><br/>Thirrin was no Arya. Not even close. I would even put her in the category of some of the worst characters I've read. Sounds drastic, but I really could not stand her. She made reading this book painful. I found her to be entirely unbelievable, even for a fanta</span>
  <span id="freeText13681902047366456735" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this book. I really did because fantasy is my favorite genre to read. The concept sounded intriguing, with a warrior girl as the lead protagonist and lots of intense battles. The idea reminded me a bit of Arya Stark.<br /><br />Thirrin was no Arya. Not even close. I would even put her in the category of some of the worst characters I've read. Sounds drastic, but I really could not stand her. She made reading this book painful. I found her to be entirely unbelievable, even for a fantasy novel. At age 13 (at the beginning of the novel anyway) she has already got the fighting skills and abilities that rival soldiers more than twice her age. I believe at one point it was mentioned that she had only started training at 10. Three years is not anywhere close to enough time to transform her into a warrior princess the way she is described. The fact she is also supposed to be capable of leading battalions the way she does as just a teenager felt ridiculous and contrived, especially when she had never seen battle before. Instead, it all came naturally to her and didn't feel like a struggle at all. Princess or not, I found it difficult to believe soldiers who were far older than her would follow a kid into battle. The fact she could garner the respect of kingdoms that had been at war for centuries made no sense either. I saw nothing that could make it believable she could gain those kingdoms as allies.<br /><br />Her arrogance and the way she treated other characters sickened me, and it didn't improve or develop through the rest of the book. Her treatment of other women in power was incredibly hypocritical. Instead of wanting to empower other women so they could be fighters like her, she sought to surround herself with men and complained, even acted hostile, when other women were assertive. I failed to see what the other characters saw in her to think she was a good ruler. The narrator made it clear we were supposed to connect with her, but she was so unbearable I saw no reason she deserved any of the admiration.<br /><br />A lot of the other problems in this book stemmed from Thirrin's character. The plot was based around the fact she was this amazing military expert and could gain the respect of different kingdoms. With the very beginning where the "were"wolf kin says he will be at Thirrin's beck and call and they would just have to trust him to keep that word when they set him free felt entirely unbelievable. Because of all those issues with Thirrin and everyone seeming to adore her, the plot didn't work and felt too thin.<br /><br />The prose itself actually wasn't the worst I've read, but unfortunately Hill failed to create a compelling protagonist or well constructed plot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13681902047366456735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_87905986" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87905986" />
    <a title="Shauna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/725210-shauna"><img alt="Shauna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234457707p2/725210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87905986?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shauna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shauna" href="/user/show/725210-shauna">Shauna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/725210-shauna?shelf=family-read-aloud">family-read-aloud</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87905986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3799933746102880483">I demoted this to two stars. The children enjoyed it for the most part, but it seemed to drag on at the end. Predictable . . . and a bit boring. It started out promising. We really liked it when Therrin punched the werewolf, and then he ended up being the king of the werewolves and eventually swore allegiance to her. But, when the 14 year old heroine takes over the country and the army when her father dies . . . it got boring and predictable. <br/><br/>Therrin is an amazing soldier and everyone defers to </span>
  <span id="freeText3799933746102880483" style="display:none">I demoted this to two stars. The children enjoyed it for the most part, but it seemed to drag on at the end. Predictable . . . and a bit boring. It started out promising. We really liked it when Therrin punched the werewolf, and then he ended up being the king of the werewolves and eventually swore allegiance to her. But, when the 14 year old heroine takes over the country and the army when her father dies . . . it got boring and predictable. <br /><br />Therrin is an amazing soldier and everyone defers to her. (Yeah, right) Here are these battle hardened soldiers, who are strong enough to defeat the Polypontian Army (based on the Roman Legions) and they look without question to the 14 year old girl? There were other parts like that. Things that don't quite fit within the context of the story. Not a good family read aloud. Too much war for 9-12 year old girls to enjoy, and too much about a girl for 9+ boys to enjoy. <br /><br />We actually did something we have NEVER done in family read aloud. We just stopped reading it near the end. (It was supposed to be climactic I think, but we were tired of reading about war preparations!) Whoever wanted to finish reading it on their own, could read it on their own and tell the rest of us about it. Amazingly, although we are only five or so chapters from the end, there were no takers. It is still in my bedtime reading basket. I guess I'll have to read the end and tell them what happens. Sheesh!<br /><br />We started reading "How to Train Your Dragon" by Cressida Cowell, right after Icemark and finished it quickly. I wouldn't quite call it a "roast beef" book, but it has a good message, and everyone was excited to read it. We even got to have extra family read aloud sessions. Whoo hoo. Gotta love that! We needed something to get everybody excited about listening again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3799933746102880483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review87905986">

  <span id="freeText637523844105276125" style="display:none">I can't even express how much I love this book! Thirrin is a fierce, temperamental princess who has to fight to save her kingdom from a Rome-like empire. She challenges previously held ideas of her people (she has to) and she thinks for herself as opposed to accepting the notions of the past. The text in this book! It's hysterical, with some of the best lines I've read and they make me laugh no matter how many times I read these books. It's also well done militarily, with enough to allow you to follow the battles but not so much to overwhelm you with positions and strategies. One of my all time favorites. </span>

<div id="review_2811454953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2811454953" />
    <a title="R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18849271-r"><img alt="R" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365895540p2/18849271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2811454953?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R" href="/user/show/18849271-r">R</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9781417779536" href="/book/show/2330599.The_Cry_of_the_Icemark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2811454953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10115050952600431425">DNF - 249/472<br/><br/>I could have finished this one. It wasn’t a difficult read and I wasn’t struggling to get through the chapters. The problem was that, every time I put the book down, I was actively looking for a reason “good enough” to not pick it back up. When that feeling hadn’t gone away by the half-way point, I officially gave up. In spite of that, I do have a rough idea how the last half of the book goes. I read this in its entirety when I was in middle school or early high school. Because of t</span>
  <span id="freeText10115050952600431425" style="display:none">DNF - 249/472<br /><br />I could have finished this one. It wasn’t a difficult read and I wasn’t struggling to get through the chapters. The problem was that, every time I put the book down, I was actively looking for a reason “good enough” to not pick it back up. When that feeling hadn’t gone away by the half-way point, I officially gave up. In spite of that, I do have a rough idea how the last half of the book goes. I read this in its entirety when I was in middle school or early high school. Because of that, I can say with confidence that the issue is not the plot. The plot is fine. The problem is that the world building, the characters, and the childish way that the plot is executed are more than enough to ruin a good plot.<br /><br />It’s far from uncommon for fantasy worlds to have some real-world inspiration. The real-world social structures of the middle ages is everywhere in fantasy. What isn’t normal is to see real cultures copy-pasted into fantasy worlds, but that’s what we have here. <br /><br />We have a tribe of people called the Hypolitan. Their society is ruled by warrior women who worship a moon goodness. So, they’re the amazons. Then there’s an empire focused on conquering the world whose words of conquest that the soldiers say before every invasion are, “Veni, vidi, vici.” So, they’re the romans. <br /><br />It’s incredibly distracting and the story would honestly have been better if the cultures were left undefined instead of using this bizarre form of plagiarism to try and make it feel like the author had created a complex world with a rich history. He hasn’t and it becomes incredibly clear as the story progresses because this lack of development goes beyond the world building. The characters are incredibly one-dimensional, too, with as little backstory as possible. <br /><br />It’s hard to fully articulate just how bland this world is, but I’ll give an example of a single interaction that illustrates the problem. Thirrin – the 14-year-old princess of the Icemark who is our leading lady – lives about a week’s ride from her mother’s people, the Hypolitan. The leader of these people is Thirrin’s aunt. At one point in the story, we get to see these two meet up. It is literally the first time they have ever met, which makes no sense. Why would Thirrin have never met her maternal family when they live so close and are the sworn allies of her father, the king? You really expect me to buy that?<br /><br />Then there’s the story itself, which is all about Thirrin having to gather an army to repel an invading force from her homeland, the Icemark. So, this is supposed to be military fantasy, but it barely qualifies. There are no complex plans or tense, but clever diplomatic interactions that allow Thirrin to build her army. Everything go Thirrin’s way with little-to-no effort on her part. Here’s an example from the first chapter of the story: Thirrin spares a werewolf’s life. That wolf turns out to be the king of the werewolf’s, so now Thirrin is allies with the werewolves without having to do much of anything. <br /><br />It’s here that we get back to my initial claim that the plot is good, but the execution is childish. The basic idea of Thirrin saving a werewolves life and that leading to an alliance is strong, but the execution is weak as cardboard. You can apply the same logic to everything that goes on here. A summary of what happens sounds like a good book, but when you actually start reading you see that every twist and development occurs with only the most basic of effort on Thirrin’s part which makes you not care. You know everything is going to work out because there’s never a set-back. <br /><br />This simplistic way of telling the story combined with the other two big issues meant that I simply wasn’t having any fun. I didn’t care to read what happened next because I already knew what would happen. I will say that I remember liking this when I first read it and I can see why a younger reader would, which is why this gets two-stars and not one. If this is your first exposure to this type of story and you’ve previously been reading more elementary literature, this definitely feels like a step-up. As someone who has read similar, but far better stories, I just couldn’t keep going.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10115050952600431425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665855904" />
    <a title="Theodosia of the Fathomless Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18279339-theodosia-of-the-fathomless-hall"><img alt="Theodosia of the Fathomless Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409783724p2/18279339.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9934091339492731003">Starting note: If you, like me stopped this book on its slow start don't give up hope for the worst...oh, wrong speech, it gets better trust me ;)<br/><br/>The Cry of the Icemark focuses on Thirrin Freer Strong-in-the-arm Lindenshield. Wildcat of the North. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Queen of the Icemark <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (which incidentally you are told in the inside flap), and her <s>boyfriend</s> adviser, Oskan, Witch's son,<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ and one of the rare Warlocks <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br/><br/>Thirrin seems nothing more than a arro</span>
  <span id="freeText9934091339492731003" style="display:none">Starting note: If you, like me stopped this book on its slow start don't give up hope for the worst...oh, wrong speech, it gets better trust me ;)<br /><br />The Cry of the Icemark focuses on Thirrin Freer Strong-in-the-arm Lindenshield. Wildcat of the North. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Queen of the Icemark <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (which incidentally you are told in the inside flap), and her <s>boyfriend</s> adviser, Oskan, Witch's son,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and one of the rare Warlocks <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Thirrin seems nothing more than a arrogant, reckless and spoiled princess for some part of the story but matures into a a less, arrogant, reckless <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[queen <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The land of the Icemark follows ye old fantasy tradition of 'alternate Europe fantasy' with the Icemark's heavily Scandinavian underpinnings and the *ahem* Empire's strangely Roman feel.<br />With titanic Snow Leopards, Vampires(not the sparkly kind!!!!) a race of tree-people of a cross between the emerging fairy genre and Elves, as well as, <i>zombies</i>. Okay. Fine. Zombies?!<br /><br />Scipio <s> Africanus</s> Bellorum is an intriguing though absolutely psycho villain but then and I was cheering on the soldier who dared to defy him - and then got shot for his troubles, dang.<br /><br />Basilea Elymnestra is a fun character and the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ last stand <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> of the Hypolitan was epicly tragic. Favorite part of the book. Full. Stop.<br />Oskan's short stint as a piece of bacon's conclusion was rather......preachy and unnecessary to me and I thought they could do it better but *shrug*<br />The concept of the Icemark and the outlaying lands was very interesting and was a major force in this book's quality.<br /><br />The battles were supremely done but the final one was very....merciless, send all the nightmare monsters after Bellorum okay!? not the soldiers that <i> saluted</i> Thirrin for god's sake! <br />Well that is my main gripe with the book but I heartily recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9934091339492731003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_308200475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308200475" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6508135-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364526836p2/6508135.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308200475?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/6508135-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308200475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3064492913936321789">This is a debut novel with strong promises that the author will hone his craft as other books come along.; but it was a first novel, and it shows. There was a lot of telling of characters' thoughts and motivations (which I tended to skip because they often went on for pages), instead of *showing* their thoughts/motives in more powerful ways. Sometimes the dangerous action, especially in the early chapters, came out of nowhere and didn't seem plausible. Moreover, I was distracted by the feeling t</span>
  <span id="freeText3064492913936321789" style="display:none">This is a debut novel with strong promises that the author will hone his craft as other books come along.; but it was a first novel, and it shows. There was a lot of telling of characters' thoughts and motivations (which I tended to skip because they often went on for pages), instead of *showing* their thoughts/motives in more powerful ways. Sometimes the dangerous action, especially in the early chapters, came out of nowhere and didn't seem plausible. Moreover, I was distracted by the feeling that I had read a lot of this book before - in other books (Dark Materials, LOTR, Narnia, and for some reason Inkheart and Stardust also kept coming to mind). This was furthered by the fact that a LOT of the names were either adapted or lifted directly from LOTR (Eodred, Icemark, Theowyn, South Farthing, etc).<br /><br />Most of the characters were strong and believable, though eclipsed at times by the bulky writing. Redrought was a bit cartoonish at times, but still very likable; and I love how Hill handled Maggie and Grimswald. ULtimately, I stuck it out through the book for Thirrin and Oskan, who were by far the most dynamic characters.<br /><br /> I think Hill was truly on to something here, it was just shrouded in the stumblings of a first book. Many of the elements - the Oak and Holly Kings, Hill's take on werewolves, the snow leopards - were truly original, as was Oskan's gifts and personal history. If the book does make it to the big screen, I expect it will be an excellent one and I"d gladly see it. I just wish that Hill had walked away from this one at the manuscript stage for about a year, taken the time to write some other things, then come back and given it the sort of brutal editing that would have taken it from mediocre to great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3064492913936321789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1207550170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14676060899501528505">A book which is clearly written for the teenage / younger market should no be dismissed out of hand because of that. My son recommended this book and so I read it and thoroughly enjoyed it while I did.<br/><br/>It was a nice change to read a book where the main character is not only a young female but one who is genuinely tough and who when forced to lead a nation does so from the front without having to ever become a victim or use her wily womanly charms. She is a full on proper heroic protagonist. I lik</span>
  <span id="freeText14676060899501528505" style="display:none">A book which is clearly written for the teenage / younger market should no be dismissed out of hand because of that. My son recommended this book and so I read it and thoroughly enjoyed it while I did.<br /><br />It was a nice change to read a book where the main character is not only a young female but one who is genuinely tough and who when forced to lead a nation does so from the front without having to ever become a victim or use her wily womanly charms. She is a full on proper heroic protagonist. I liked that a lot. Nuanced as well, at no point did I feel the author short changed any of his characters.<br /><br />The book treads a fairly well worn path and does so at a breakneck pace so that the reader can never get bored. It it within pages of the start of the book that the hero faces her first challenge and from that moment on she never stops. <br /><br />There could have been more time spent in this book. On occasion I felt there was undue haste in barrelling through the tale but then in the classic 50s sci-fi that was necessary to capture and keep the reader.<br /><br />I liked the fact this book had a proper ending, I liked all the main characters in the book and the baddie was a fully formed figure as well. The story was satisfying and fun with loads of action. Had I read it at my sons age I too would have loved it. It was good to see him reading and enjoying the book and it is one I have recommended to friends with daughters as well just because it is rare to see such a positive female role model allowed to sit at the very centre of a high adventure fantasy novel. <br /><br />This is not a girl's book, it is an everyone’s book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14676060899501528505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49513130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49513130?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aneuwoman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aneuwoman" href="/user/show/1392703-aneuwoman">Aneuwoman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439686266" href="/book/show/1292327.The_Cry_of_the_Icemark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer49513130&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49513130" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13589479964849537195">I love fantasy books and this one definitely delivered on the goods. I love girls who can fight and Hill made me proud by creating such a courageous heroine in Thirrin. She is so young and yet so responsible. She is definitely a positive role model for young women. Even though she is 14, Thirrin isn't boy-crazy or pretentious. She's not even a "girly-girl". Instead, she is a mini-clone of her father. She is a warrior with a conscious. While the book was a little slow in reaching its climax, I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13589479964849537195" style="display:none">I love fantasy books and this one definitely delivered on the goods. I love girls who can fight and Hill made me proud by creating such a courageous heroine in Thirrin. She is so young and yet so responsible. She is definitely a positive role model for young women. Even though she is 14, Thirrin isn't boy-crazy or pretentious. She's not even a "girly-girl". Instead, she is a mini-clone of her father. She is a warrior with a conscious. While the book was a little slow in reaching its climax, I was moved by the emotional risks that the author took along the way. He made me feel as if my heart was ripped out when King Redrought was slain. But since this book is a lesson on courage and bravery, my girl, Thirrin takes it all in stride. Loss after loss, stressful situation after stressful situation, she rises again and again to meet her challenges head on. She's not devoid of emotion; she's full of emotion and passion, but is almost never ruled by them. She definitely makes a solid case for women as monarchs. And I love the Hypolitan women and their society in which the roles between men and women are completely reversed! Go girls, you all rocked! The soldiers are fiercesome and skillful. I was crushed when the archers were cut down during the battle for Frostmarris. They were such a deadly threat. I would have loved to have been a Hypolitan citizen. How come women don't write stories like this. Major points scored for Stuart Hill (and other male authors who write such strong roles for women).</span>
  <a data-text-id="13589479964849537195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1732788288774019276">I really struggled through this one. The characters didn't engage me and failed to make that connection that makes a reader care what happens to them. There was no character development and from the beginning the adult characters acted and sounded too much like children. I understand the two main characters are 14 and 15 and in charge of everyone else but still the adult supporting characters I'd expect to act like adults and live up to their role as <i>Supporting Characters</i>, in more ways than one.</span>
  <span id="freeText1732788288774019276" style="display:none">I really struggled through this one. The characters didn't engage me and failed to make that connection that makes a reader care what happens to them. There was no character development and from the beginning the adult characters acted and sounded too much like children. I understand the two main characters are 14 and 15 and in charge of everyone else but still the adult supporting characters I'd expect to act like adults and live up to their role as <i>Supporting Characters</i>, in more ways than one. Instead they end up getting consoled most of the time by kids, or bullied by them.<br /> Then there was Thirrin who's a 14 year old princess. She was arrogant, childish in all aspects but war, full of herself and antagonistic to anyone else who had some semblance of authority and of the female persuasion. (Looking back the only males with authority she had a problem with were the antagonist who was threatening her country and one of her allies who was married.) Seriously there was one scene where she picks a fight with an elderly witch woman who's the elder and leader of the witches. True the witch wasn't all sunshine and rainbows either but really I was expecting Thirrin to get slapped for her behavior instead she gets bowed to and proclaimed a strong leader after a drawn out rather immature shouting match of thrown insults. No one stands up to her and she came off as more of a huge bully than a young leader of a nation. I didn't find her likable at all. I realize this is a childrens book and it's not bad but it isn't great either. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1732788288774019276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_90439382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90439382" />
    <a title="Ashton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/154454-ashton"><img alt="Ashton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1185127090p2/154454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90439382?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashton" href="/user/show/154454-ashton">Ashton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90439382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14466250586322987393">I really enjoyed this one. I've had it for a couple of years (given by a friend) and never got around to reading it until yesterday. It was fun, engaging, and keeps you interested the whole way. I am looking forward to the sequels to arrive at my library so I can pick them up!<br/><br/>Hill uses an interesting mix of the British and Roman Empires to model the Polypontians on - down to "vini vidi vici" being their announcement and so forth. Some of the parallels made me groan, but not for long. The story o</span>
  <span id="freeText14466250586322987393" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this one. I've had it for a couple of years (given by a friend) and never got around to reading it until yesterday. It was fun, engaging, and keeps you interested the whole way. I am looking forward to the sequels to arrive at my library so I can pick them up!<br /><br />Hill uses an interesting mix of the British and Roman Empires to model the Polypontians on - down to "vini vidi vici" being their announcement and so forth. Some of the parallels made me groan, but not for long. The story of Thirrin and Oskan was interesting and it was a good version of the teenager suddenly ruling a kingdom. Battle scenes are really good - the descriptions are very clear, and give you a great mental image, which is unique. Many battle scenes in fantasy books leave you lost so you end up gathering details like who got killed and so forth rather than being able to see what actually happened.But here I could envisualize the city and how the fortifications were put together. Also, the voice the story is told in is unique. He swaps between characters without being obnoxious - so it's third person, but, in a good way. Recommend this for a fun read, for sure. I wouldn't quite put it down as a milkshake book, but it's close. Definitely fun to read, definitely good, definitely not the first time someone has told this story, but it was enjoyable to go to a new place.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14466250586322987393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review90439382">

<div id="review_103636210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103636210" />
    <a title="Jessi Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2078631-jessi-brown"><img alt="Jessi Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296269449p2/2078631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103636210?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi Brown" href="/user/show/2078631-jessi-brown">Jessi Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439686266" href="/book/show/1292327.The_Cry_of_the_Icemark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2078631-jessi-brown?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2078631-jessi-brown?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103636210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer284453587564893071">Cry of the Icemark is the story of young Thirrin, a warrior princess to the land of Icemark. Shortly after her 14th birthday, she is officially made heir to the throne in the case of her father's death. Soon after, an army from the south begins to invade north towards Icemark hoping to overtake the small land and claim it as its own. After her father's brave death in battle Thirrin is then faced with the large responsibility of Queen. Knowing she cannot defeat the invading army she reaches out t</span>
  <span id="freeText284453587564893071" style="display:none">Cry of the Icemark is the story of young Thirrin, a warrior princess to the land of Icemark. Shortly after her 14th birthday, she is officially made heir to the throne in the case of her father's death. Soon after, an army from the south begins to invade north towards Icemark hoping to overtake the small land and claim it as its own. After her father's brave death in battle Thirrin is then faced with the large responsibility of Queen. Knowing she cannot defeat the invading army she reaches out to the most unlikely sources for allies involving the Wolf-folk, the King and Queen of the Vampires, and the Snow Leopards. <br />This book has the coming of age quality that one would look for in a young adult novel, Thirrin tends to be very unsure of herself at times stating that she hopes people don't notice that she's making this up as she goes. Along with Thirrin is a Warlock who is her age, her Royal Advisor, and must face his decision of turning to the light or the dark. I found the battle scenes quite vivid, and the tension between technology and the unknown thought-provoking. Overall, I didn't love this book, but I didn't hate it either. </span>
  <a data-text-id="284453587564893071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11675067233182280874">The Icemark is a kingdom in grave danger. Its king has been killed in battle, its enemy lies in wait, and its fate rests on the shoulders of Thirrin Freer Strong-in-the-Arm Lindenshield, a beautiful princess and an intrepid warrior, who must find a way to protect her land from a terrible invasion. She will forge an extraordinary alliance of noble Snow Leopards, ancient Vampires, and ferocious Wolf-folk. She will find unexpected strength in her friendship with a young warlock. And she will lead h</span>
  <span id="freeText11675067233182280874" style="display:none">The Icemark is a kingdom in grave danger. Its king has been killed in battle, its enemy lies in wait, and its fate rests on the shoulders of Thirrin Freer Strong-in-the-Arm Lindenshield, a beautiful princess and an intrepid warrior, who must find a way to protect her land from a terrible invasion. She will forge an extraordinary alliance of noble Snow Leopards, ancient Vampires, and ferocious Wolf-folk. She will find unexpected strength in her friendship with a young warlock. And she will lead her allies to victory with her fierce battle cry: "Blood! Blast! And Fire!"<br /><br />What I like about this book is the excitement it gives the reader while the plot unfolds and the authors craftiness in the way he portrayed the alliances, in particular. He used a very diverse selection and some well known mythical creatures like vampires and ware wolves and warlocks. The way he makes the reader feel like he/she knows Thirrin is just incredible. Overall this is an amazingly well written book with a lot of evidence of thoughtfulness.<br /><br /></span>
